< Text>
Eight Tables is just a phenomenal restaurant. Everything about it from the moment you walk in, the ambiance really hits you. Then the fact that there are eight tables makes it an interesting atmosphere in the restaurant. The service was very accommodating and even realized that my brother was a lefty. The food was outstanding. Starting with a very varietal first course that brought flavors that were shared in later courses. The chefs table in the kitchen gave my family a good chance to see what goes on in this hectic kitchen. It was quite clean and very organized. Overall this is probably one of the best restaurants I have ever been too and I‚Äôm bound to come again.</Text>

< Text>
This was the best dinner of my life!  My two girls and I are so lucky to have enjoyed an amazingly fantastic meal here. And as fortunate as we are to have one of the few tables at Eight Tables by George Chen, we were even more blessed to be able to eat inside the kitchen at this incredible restaurant.

The food is beyond comparison and the Chef‚Äôs Table gave us front row seats to the stage where the magic happens. We also received a  history lesson about Chinese culture as well as an education in wine that was shared with passion and enthusiasm.

I don‚Äôt think any of us will forget this night. Here are photos of the food.</Text>

Maria Smith<//Name>
<Date>1538293833026< /Date><rate>5<//rate><review>This is our second Michelin rated restaurant we have tried. Eight Tables deserves the star. This is a culinary experience! We ordered the Chef's Menu ($325 per person, 12 courses), not the main menu ($225 per person) which includes 2 more courses than the main menu (10 courses). Chef George Chen beautifully creates and builds up each course. The textures and flavors are amazing! Not one course disappointed. By the ninth course, you start feeling full. The service is the best we have ever received- uber attentive and synchronized. Even though this restaurant is expensive, the staff is down to earth. We celebrated my husband's birthday here- it definitely was a gift. Chef George Chen visits every table to welcome his guests and explains the first course. When you first arrive, you are not really sure where the entrance is, but the valet person unlocks the gate and escorts you to the entrance of the "house". You take the elevator to the second floor. Chef George Chen wants you to feel like you're at his home. It's a dining experience of a lifetime.<//review>< pictures>

< review>
The best restaurant experience I've had so far. We got lucky and got moved to the chef's table in the kitchen. The food was delicious and we ordered the extra dishes like the A5 wagyu. We had the usual 10 course menu and we added the abalone and A5 wagyu beef and broccoli.

We also had a great durian cocktail that was super delicious.</review>

< text>
Impeccable! Though a new spot in town, it looks like the people are giving Eight Tables two thumbs up. My thumbs are sore from being held up for Chef George Chen too.

I usually don't go for $$$$ Chinese food, because I always feel ripped off afterwards when my mom could have cooked a meal for a fraction of the price and 100x the taste. However, Eight Tables was one of a few exceptions where the food, combined with experience, is worth every penny. I can't wait to see a Michelin star or two soon for you, which is inevitable. Just glad I got to visit before it becomes impossible to get a reservation!

If you want an overview of the magic, just look at my pictures. The evening was beautiful and nothing short of perfection, and you get to learn a little bit about Chinese history along the way too.</text>

< text>
What a great meal! Service was really excellent. I took my mom for her birthday, and all the staff stopped by to greet her. A few of the Cantonese speaking wait staff also made an attempt to talk to us and describe some of the dishes.

Everything was presented beautifully and most dishes were really tasty. Especially liked the fish dish (forgot the name now). Everyone starts with the Jiu Gong Ge (nine essential flavors) which was a really nice introduction to the meal. The desserts fell a bit flat but overall the meal was great.

Would definitely recommend this for a special occasion. Love that they highlight Chinese cuisine in a refined manner.</text>

<time>1507000747857< /time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< text>
I went back for a second visit and found the food and service to be just as outstanding as my first visit. They added a new mushroom/pea leaves/ bean sprout dish whose flavors and contrasting textures really popped. The juicy crunch of the pea leaves (often tough in other restaurants) and bean sprouts provided a perfect foil to the buttery shiitakes (in maggi sauce, I think). Previous favorite dishes like the velvet chicken, hongshao pork, crunchy fried rice, marinated clam, foie gras dumpling with tuile, Napa cabbage purse, sea grass prawn, iberico charsiu, sesame basil mochi, etc were once again flawless in execution. The amount of labor required to produce these dishes must be mind boggling. The staff and sommelier were a pleasure to deal with and the cocktails and desserts were exceptional. Pro tip: skip lunch before coming here.</text>

<Resp>None</Resp>< review>
We have dined here for more than 40 years and my parents and neighbours since the day it opened.
I have never had a major complaint regarding our food or service, until now. My wife (who has only been there with me three times made a reservation for my birthday. She made it for a Sunday night and the manager (or whoever she was) even called back to get a time as she had not noted it before. We arrived and was surprised that the restaurant was closed! Obviously, there was some misunderstanding, so we ended up elsewhere. My wife E-Mailed the restaurant explaining what happened and how disappointed we were. After a few days of receiving no reply, I called the restaurant tonight. I asked to speak with the manager, the woman (with a marked french accent) asked how she could help me. I  to explain what had happened... honestly, I was more upset that had failed to reply to the E-Mail than I was for the reservation... before I could finish my sentence she yelled at me that NO ONE TOOK SUCH A RESERVATION... IT DID NOT HAPPEN. WE ARE CLOSED SUNDAY & MONDAY and no one would have taken such a reservation.  We must have made it at another restaurant as there is one with the similar name on Ventura Blvd. I tried to explain that we had come there for years so we certainly knew which place my wife was calling... in fact my wife recognized her voice from the time she called to make the reservation. She was shouting so loud that my wife could hear her through the phone.
I told that her attitude to yell a long time customer (or ANY customer for that matter) was just plain wrong. She replied again "it did not happen, all of our staff have been here for more than 30 years and no one would make such a mistake! I told that her attitude was appalling and after 40 years we would not be back... she said thank you and hung up. I guess she is without fault and is perfect as we know that SHE took the reservation. I was not seeking any compensation for the mistake, just a simple apology. Truthfully, they should have responded to the E-Mail in the first place. Then this phone conversation would never have occurred
There are too many fine dining establishments in Los Angeles for a place to adopt such an arrogant attitude... many places that have been in business for 40 + years have gone by the wayside.< /review>

<userid>111870059074343499111</userid><name>Desmond Forden<//name><time>1575560035057< /time><rate>4< /rate>< review>
I hadn't heard of Bottlecraft until a coworker had suggested a happy hour here recently and well, you know how it is - I'm not longer surprised that these breweries are located in the once empty commercial spaces in San Diego. Since we're the capital of microbreweries now it only makes sense. Don't get me wrong, it's great to have it as a local industry, and Bottlecraft is a great member of that.

The space isn't to crowded and pretty modern. It has warm glow and had what I like to call a Euro/Ikea feel. In a good way. Reading the list of beers was a bit overwhelming as to me each seemed like a custom creation from a smaller brewery experimenting. I'm totally down with that. I can't remember exactly which beer I had but the addition of watermelon sold me. It was easily drinkable and enjoyable! So the bottom line is there's lots to choose from and the space is clean and simple. Definitely my kind of hangout.< /review>

<Response>None<//Response>< Review>
On a good note; the girl that took our order was very pleasant, and the fries were really good.

Now the rest; we ordered 3 meals.  Country fried steak with sunnyside up eggs, spicey chicken sandwich meal and a double cheeseburger meal.

Country fried steak was so overcooked it couldnt be cut into, leather like.  The breading was burnt.
Spicey chicken sandwich was also burnt tasting and hard to chew.
The double cheeseburger was cold, completely dried out and tasted like charcoal.  The cheese must've been an afterthought because it wasn't even melted.

We gave our remaining food to our dog, even she turned up her nose.

We waited for OVER an hour for this meal.
It's really hard to support locally (especially in Mojave) with this kind of lack of service and pride.
Sadly, we should've just went to McDonald's.

Guess it's worth it to drive for good food.<//Review>
